  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>This is the followup to <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DERBY-1823" title="Derby Developer's Guide -  Issues w/ User authentication and authorization extended examples section/paragraph" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="DERBY-1823"><del>DERBY-1823</del></a> that Francois Orsini suggested.</p> 
                  <p>I've been experimenting and reading the Developer's Guide section on SQL authorization (User authorizations, cdevcsecure36595).</p> 
                  <p>It appears that the only use of SQL authorization mode is to restrict user access, not to expand it.</p> 
                  <p>For example, if you set the default connection mode to noAccess, a user with fullAccess can't grant any privileges to a user with noAccess. And presumably if the default connection mode is readOnlyAccess, a user with fullAccess can't grant any privileges beyond SELECT, which the user has anyway.</p> 
                  <p>Only if the default connection mode is fullAccess is SQL authorization mode meaningful. That means that a fullAccess user can use GRANT to restrict another user's privileges on a particular database that the user owns.</p> 
                  <p>I'm running into a problem at the end, though. At the beginning of the program, as nobody in particular, I was able to create several users, some of them with full access. But at the end of the program, it seems that even a user with full access isn't allowed to turn off those database properties:</p> 
                  <p>Message: User 'MARY' does not have execute permission on PROCEDURE 'SYSCS_UTIL'.'SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY'.</p> 
                  <p>This seems a bit extreme. I know that with SQL authorization on, "the ability to read from or write to database objects is further restricted to the owner of the database objects." But the ability to execute built-in system procedures? Can I log in as SYSCS_UTIL? How? </p> 
                  <p>I realize that having access to SYSCS_SET_DATABASE_PROPERTY would allow me to in effect delete myself – but that's essentially what I do at the end of the program that sets derby.connection.requireAuthentication but not derby.database.sqlAuthorization. </p> 
                  <p>The documentation does say that once you have turned on SQL authorization, you can't turn it off. But it doesn't say that you can't turn anything else off, either!</p> 
                  <p>I'll attach the program I've been using. Most of the stacktraces are expected, but I'm stumped by that last one.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

identifier when creating the database.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSince you didn\'t specify a user at the original connect that created the database, this defaults to user \\\"APP\\\".\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eChanging owner to user mary, which is the effective user you have when trying to switch things off, will make it work:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e Wanvik\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12542190_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'13\\/Nov\\/07 18:20\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2007-11-13T18:20:38+0000\'\u003e13\\/Nov\\/07 18:20\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    The problem is that only the database owner can call that procedure once you have set sqlAuthorization to true. \\nThis is to avoid a security hole: Otherwise any user could gain access by switching sqlAuthorization off. \\n\\n The database owner here is the effective user authorization identifier when creating the database. \\nSince you didn\'t specify a user at the original connect that created the database, this defaults to user \\\"APP\\\". \\n\\n Changing owner to user mary, which is the effective user you have when trying to switch things off, will make it work: \\n\\n         String connectionURL = \\\"jdbc:derby:\\\" + dbName + \\\";user=mary;create=true\\\"; \\n\\n Hope this helps                \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Wanvik\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12585079_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'03\\/Apr\\/08 12:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-04-03T12:33:00+0000\'\u003e03\\/Apr\\/08 12:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Some comments on the initial description section. \\n\\n &gt; For example, if you set the default connection mode to noAccess, a \\n&gt; user with fullAccess can\'t grant any privileges to a user with \\n&gt; noAccess.  \\n\\n I guess he could, but it would be of little use, since the noAccess \\nwould override the privilege. \\n\\n &gt; And presumably if the default connection mode is readOnlyAccess, a \\n&gt; user with fullAccess can\'t grant any privileges beyond SELECT,  \\n\\n Again, the full access user could grant update privilege but it would \\nbe of no use, since the grantee and only read (connection level \\nauthorization overrides again). \\n\\n &gt; which the user has anyway. \\n\\n No, that is not the case: when sqlAuthorization mode is active, a user \\nonly has access to her own tables by default (and read access to \\nsystem tables it seems). \\n\\n Cf section \\\"How user authorization properties work together\\\" in the \\ndev guide:  \\n\\n (quote) \\n\\n \\n\\t The access mode specified for the \\n  derby.database.defaultConnectionMode property overrides the \\n  permissions that are granted by the owner of a database object. For \\n  example, if a user is granted INSERT privileges on a table but the \\n  user only has read-only connection authorization, the user cannot \\n  insert data into the table. \\n \\n\\n\\n I interpret this \\\"overrides\\\" as \\\"further restricts\\\". \\n\\n &gt; Only if the default connection mode is fullAccess is SQL authorization \\n&gt; mode meaningful.  \\n\\n No, even for connections with readOnly connection access, the \\nGRANT\\/REVOKE machinery can be used to further limit access (but not to \\nbroaden it beyond readOnly). \\n\\n &gt; That means that a fullAccess user can use GRANT to restrict another \\n&gt; user\'s privileges on a particular database that the user owns. \\n\\n GRANT\\/REVOKE provides more fine graned access control that connection \\nlevel authorization. The way I think of this is that, when both are \\nused, the more limiting access provided by each authorization \\nmechanism (connection or sqlAUthorization) rules the day in any \\nparticular case. \\n\\n Hope this makes sense   It is a bit confusing, so making running \\nexamples to check understanding is very useful here. \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12600801_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'29\\/May\\/08 15:34\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-05-29T15:34:08+0000\'\u003e29\\/May\\/08 15:34\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThanks very much, Dag, for the help! \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI have now put in code to shut down the database at the end of the first client program. I am trying to make these as similar as possible in structure to the client built-in authentication\\/authorization programs under \u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/db.apache.org\\/derby\\/docs\\/dev\\/devguide\\/devguide-single.html#rdevcsecure125\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/db.apache.org\\/derby\\/docs\\/dev\\/devguide\\/devguide-single.html#rdevcsecure125\u003c\\/a\u003e. I no longer remember why we had the two programs in that section &#8211; maybe to show that you can continue to run the Derby engine while running more than one program? I am not sure why those two programs work fine when you don\'t shut down the database between the first and second programs &#8211; because they set some static properties too (derby.connection.requireAuthentication). Maybe they aren\'t working fine after all, though they seem to be doing the right things.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo now when I shut down the database at the end of the first program and connect at the start of the second, everything works the same way the built-in authentication\\/authorization programs do &#8211; until the very end.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e(The reason I put in the comment about the defaultConnectionMode being fullAccess was that previously, if I didn\'t shut down the database, I was allowed to log in without a username or password, as if the default connection mode really was fullAccess. But that is no longer the case.)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWhat happens at the end is that I cannot shut down the database &#8211; I get an authentication failure. (I also can\'t call the SYSCS_UTIL procedures.) I realize that only the owner of the database can shut it down if SQL authorization is on &#8211; so who was I when I created the database, and how do I become that user again? I think I was APP &#8211; the authorized user for both the APP and SYSCS_UTIL schemas according to the output of the \\\"select * from sys.sysschemas\\\" statement:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eij&gt; select * from sys.sysschemas;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSCHEMAID                            |SCHEMANAME                                                                                                                      |AUTHORIZATIONID\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n...\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nc013800d-00fb-2649-07ec-000000134f30|SYSCS_UTIL                                                                                                                      |APP                                                                                                                             \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n80000000-00d2-b38f-4cda-000a0a412c00|APP                                                                                                                             |APP                                                                                                                             \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n0ddd00a9-011a-351d-3249-ffffd494cc61|MARY                                                                                                                            |MARY\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut how would I connect to the database as the user \\\"APP\\\"? What is APP\'s password? I tried using APP123 (that was the password for Service Registry\'s Java DB instance) but I got authentication errors. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI tried calling \\\"SET SCHEMA APP\\\" before shutting down the database, but that had no effect either.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI then tried creating the database as the user who will eventually shut it down (mary), but that user cannot call the SYSCS_UTIL procedures to set the database properties. So there seems to be a catch-22: you have to be APP to create a database and users and set SQL authorization; but then you can\'t seem to revert to that user in order to shut down the database.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'m attaching the files in their current state for you to try out. I am trying to make these as similar as possible in structure to the client built-in authentication\\/authorization programs under  http:\\/\\/db.apache.org\\/derby\\/docs\\/dev\\/devguide\\/devguide-single.html#rdevcsecure125 . I no longer remember why we had the two programs in that section &#8211; maybe to show that you can continue to run the Derby engine while running more than one program? I am not sure why those two programs work fine when you don\'t shut down the database between the first and second programs &#8211; because they set some static properties too (derby.connection.requireAuthentication). Maybe they aren\'t working fine after all, though they seem to be doing the right things. \\n\\n So now when I shut down the database at the end of the first program and connect at the start of the second, everything works the same way the built-in authentication\\/authorization programs do &#8211; until the very end. \\n\\n (The reason I put in the comment about the defaultConnectionMode being fullAccess was that previously, if I didn\'t shut down the database, I was allowed to log in without a username or password, as if the default connection mode really was fullAccess. But that is no longer the case.) \\n\\n What happens at the end is that I cannot shut down the database &#8211; I get an authentication failure. (I also can\'t call the SYSCS_UTIL procedures.) I realize that only the owner of the database can shut it down if SQL authorization is on &#8211; so who was I when I created the database, and how do I become that user again? I think I was APP &#8211; the authorized user for both the APP and SYSCS_UTIL schemas according to the output of the \\\"select * from sys.sysschemas\\\" statement: \\n\\n ij&gt; select * from sys.sysschemas; \\nSCHEMAID                            |SCHEMANAME                                                                                                                      |AUTHORIZATIONID \\n... \\nc013800d-00fb-2649-07ec-000000134f30|SYSCS_UTIL                                                                                                                      |APP                                                                                                                              \\n80000000-00d2-b38f-4cda-000a0a412c00|APP                                                                                                                             |APP                                                                                                                              \\n0ddd00a9-011a-351d-3249-ffffd494cc61|MARY                                                                                                                            |MARY \\n\\n But how would I connect to the database as the user \\\"APP\\\"? What is APP\'s password? I tried using APP123 (that was the password for Service Registry\'s Java DB instance) but I got authentication errors.  \\n\\n I tried calling \\\"SET SCHEMA APP\\\" before shutting down the database, but that had no effect either. \\n\\n I then tried creating the database as the user who will eventually shut it down (mary), but that user cannot call the SYSCS_UTIL procedures to set the database properties. So there seems to be a catch-22: you have to be APP to create a database and users and set SQL authorization; but then you can\'t seem to revert to that user in order to shut down the database. \\n\\n I\'m attaching the files in their current state for you to try out. Wanvik\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12602137_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'04\\/Jun\\/08 01:11\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-06-04T01:11:14+0000\'\u003e04\\/Jun\\/08 01:11\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eKim &gt; Should I modify the topics that say the default connection mode is fullAccess, to say that when SQL authorization is on the default is null?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHmm, this is a bit tricky to explain. We have two authorization systems that work in conjunction. The connection level authorization and the SQL authorization (if enabled).  When SQL authorization is enabled, this \u003cb\u003efurther restricts\u003c\\/b\u003e whatever restrictions are in place by the connection level authorization (and vice versa). That is, for a user that has full access connection level access, she cannot update a table owned by someone else (unless she is the database owner, or has been granted the relevant SQL permission). If a user has read only connection level authorization, she can not \u003cb\u003eread\u003c\\/b\u003e another user\'s tables (unless ... as before). But in this case, she cannot update the tables \u003cb\u003eeven if\u003c\\/b\u003e suitable SQL level access has been granted. So, the most restrictive authorization \\\"wins\\\", if you will...\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nSo, the default for the connection level authorization (fullAccess) still applies even in the presence of SQL authorization, but it is no carte blanche...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHope this helps...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dagw\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12602137_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dagw\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dagw\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Dag H. Wanvik\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12602137_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'04\\/Jun\\/08 01:11\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-06-04T01:11:14+0000\'\u003e04\\/Jun\\/08 01:11\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Kim &gt; Should I modify the topics that say the default connection mode is fullAccess, to say that when SQL authorization is on the default is null? \\n\\n Hmm, this is a bit tricky to explain. We have two authorization systems that work in conjunction. The connection level authorization and the SQL authorization (if enabled).  When SQL authorization is enabled, this  further restricts  whatever restrictions are in place by the connection level authorization (and vice versa). That is, for a user that has full access connection level access, she cannot update a table owned by someone else (unless she is the database owner, or has been granted the relevant SQL permission). If a user has read only connection level authorization, she can not  read  another user\'s tables (unless ... as before). But in this case, she cannot update the tables  even if  suitable SQL level access has been granted. So, the most restrictive authorization \\\"wins\\\", if you will... \\nSo, the default for the connection level authorization (fullAccess) still applies even in the presence of SQL authorization, but it is no carte blanche... \\n\\n Hope this helps... \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n I have been looking at this new code, and I am a bit puzzled by what happens when we try to shut down the database in embedded mode. It appears  not  to raise a SQLException. I modified the code slightly so that something is printed out no matter what happens: \\n\\n             boolean gotSQLExc = false; \\n            try  \\n{\\n                DriverManager.getConnection(\\\"jdbc:derby:authEmbDB;shutdown=true\\\");\\n            }\\n  catch (SQLException se) { \\n                if ( se.getSQLState().equals(\\\"08006\\\") )  \\n{\\n                    gotSQLExc = true;\\n                }\\n  else  \\n{\\n                    errorPrint(se);\\n                }\\n             } \\n\\n             if (!gotSQLExc)  \\n{\\n                 System.out.println(\\n                     \\\"Database did not shut down normally\\\");\\n            }\\n  else  \\n{\\n                 System.out.println(\\\"Database shut down normally\\\");\\n            }\\n\\n The only output is the line \\\"Database did not shut down normally\\\", indicating that the exception wasn\'t raised. An exception is raised when you shut down the database in Network Server mode but apparently not in embedded mode. I don\'t know if the database was actually shut down or not.               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n I\'ve added a method that closes the connection and shuts down the database, which is called if unexpected errors occur as well as at the end of the programs. \\n\\n Some offline consultation with Dag has led to another change. Instead of turning off the security properties at the end of each program, it seems best to model the behavior we want to see in real-world examples and to leave the properties set on each database when we exit the program. This has the side effect of shortening some very long examples. \\n\\n The only drawback is that the documentation of how to turn off Derby properties is spotty &#8211; these examples were the main illustration of it, I think. Setting a property value to null in effect restores the built-in default setting for that property. This information needs to be added to the description of Derby properties in the Tuning Guide, probably in the topic \\\"Derby properties\\\" ( http:\\/\\/db.apache.org\\/derby\\/docs\\/dev\\/tuning\\/ctunproper22250.html ). The behavior for turning off user settings is slightly different and is documented in several places; it\'s the general case that seems to be missing. I will create a JIRA issue for this. \\n\\n New versions of sample programs to follow.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n
